## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: solid mechanics / materials science (thermoelasticity and constitutive stress–strain–temperature modeling)
**Analysis**: The variables (sigma stress, epsilon strain, T temperature) indicate a constitutive law for material response, where stress depends on mechanical strain and temperature via elastic modulus changes, thermal expansion (stress-free strain shift), and possible yielding/hardening with thermal softening.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Linear Hooke’s law (isothermal small-strain elasticity): sigma = c0 * epsilon (elastic regime with constant modulus)
- Thermal-offset linear thermoelasticity: sigma = c0 * (epsilon - c1 * (T - c2)) (stress from mechanical strain relative to thermal strain; c1 ~ thermal expansion coefficient, c0 ~ modulus)
- Temperature-dependent modulus (affine in temperature): sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon (elastic modulus varies approximately linearly with T over limited range)
- Exponential thermal softening of modulus: sigma = c0 * exp(c1 * T) * epsilon (modulus changes strongly with temperature; c1 often negative for softening)
- Nonlinear elastic polynomial (Landau-type expansion): sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**2 + c2 * epsilon**3 (moderate-strain nonlinearity without explicit plasticity)
- Cubic nonlinearity with temperature coupling: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * T * epsilon + c2 * epsilon**3 (temperature-modulated tangent stiffness plus nonlinear elasticity)
- Ramberg–Osgood (implicit stress–strain; explicit in sigma as approximation): sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * Abs(epsilon)**c2 * Sign(epsilon) (captures smooth transition from linear to power-law hardening in monotonic loading)
- Power-law hardening with thermal softening of strength: sigma = (c0 * exp(c1 * T)) + c2 * Abs(epsilon)**c3 (temperature-dependent base strength plus strain hardening)
- Elastic–plastic with yield plateau (smooth approximation): sigma = c0 * epsilon - c1 * log(1 + exp(c2 * (c3 * epsilon - c4 * exp(c5 * T)))) (smoothly limits stress growth near a temperature-dependent yield point)
- Hyperelastic (neo-Hookean-like small-strain proxy): sigma = c0 * (epsilon + c1 * epsilon**2) / (1 + c2 * epsilon) (rational form capturing stiffening/softening with strain)
- Thermal stress under constrained strain: sigma = c0 * (c1 - c2 * (T - c3)) (epsilon effectively fixed at c1; stress varies with T due to thermal expansion mismatch)
- Separable scaling (empirical constitutive surface): sigma = c0 * (Abs(epsilon) + c1)**c2 * (T + c3)**c4 * Sign(epsilon) (fit form for broad regimes with multiplicative strain/temperature effects)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Small-strain elastic regime → sigma approximately proportional to epsilon (linear dependence with slope = tangent modulus).
- Thermal expansion introduces a stress-free strain shift → dependence on (epsilon - c*(T - T0)) rather than epsilon alone.
- Thermal softening/stiffening of modulus → multiplicative temperature factor on epsilon, e.g., E(T)*epsilon with E(T) often decreasing smoothly with T (polynomial or exponential).
- Nonlinear elasticity at moderate strain → odd-power terms in epsilon (e.g., epsilon**3) add symmetric stiffening/softening without invoking plasticity.
- Yielding/flow onset → transition from linear growth to slower growth or capped slope; represented by smooth log/softplus-type transitions or piecewise-like constructs in epsilon.
- Strain hardening in plastic regime → sigma grows like Abs(epsilon)**n (power-law) after yield; combining with temperature captures thermal softening of strength.
- Tension–compression symmetry vs asymmetry → use Sign(epsilon) and Abs(epsilon) to enforce symmetric response, or omit them to allow asymmetric behavior.
- Wide-range empirical fits often factorize → sigma ≈ f(epsilon)*g(T) when temperature mainly rescales stiffness/strength rather than changing curve shape.

`T*c0*(c1 + epsilon)^3 + c2*epsilon + c3*exp(c4*epsilon) + c5*epsilon + c6`

With c4≠0, exp(c4*epsilon) is not polynomial. Can't match. With c4=0:
`T*c0*c1^3 + 3*T*c0*c1^2*epsilon + 3*T*c0*c1*epsilon^2 + T*c0*epsilon^3 + (c2+c5)*epsilon + (c3+c6)`

From T*epsilon^3: c0 = 4.278
From T*epsilon^2: 3*c0*c1 = 0 → c1 = 0
But then T*epsilon: 3*c0*c1^2 = 0 ✓
T: c0*c1^3 = 0, but GT needs -0.2857 for T coefficient. **No match** confirmed.
